          In this section, we offer a brief overview of the TWAS methods used in
          our analysis, which will be further explored through our regression
          framework (refer to the cited articles for more details). For clarity,
          we denote $\mathbf{y}$ as a vector containing the centered traits for
          $n$ individuals. The predicted expression for each gene across all
          individuals in tissue $l$ is represented by $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$,
          calculated as the sum of weighted genotype values $X_a$ and their
          corresponding weights $w_{a}^{l}$ from tissue prediction model $l$.
          Subsequently, we standardize $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$ to obtain
          $\mathbf{t}_l$, with a mean of zero and standard deviation of one.


          [Equation 1]: $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l = \sum_{a \in \mathrm{model}_l}
          w_{a}^{l} X_a$


          [Equation 2]: $\mathbf{t}_l = \frac{\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l -
          \mu_l}{\sigma_l}$


          Where:

          - $\mu_l$: mean of the predicted expression for tissue $l$

          - $\sigma_l$: standard deviation of the predicted expression for
          tissue $l$


          References:

          [@pmid:33931583; @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]

          In this section, we outline the essential aspects of the TWAS methods
          that will be relevant for our regression analysis (refer to the cited
          articles for further details). The following definitions are provided
          for clarity:


          1. $\mathbf{y}$ denotes a centered vector of traits for $n$
          individuals, implying no intercept is required.

          2. $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l = \sum\limits_{a \in \mathrm{model}_l}
          w_{a}^{l} X_{a}$ represents the predicted gene expression for all
          individuals in tissue $l$. Here, $X_a$ signifies the genotype of SNP
          $a$, and $w_{a}^{l}$ is its corresponding weight in the tissue
          prediction model $l$.

          3. The standardized version of $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$, denoted as
          $\mathbf{t}_l$, has a mean of zero and a standard deviation of one.


          Equations:

          1. $\mathbf{y} = [y_1, y_2, ..., y_n]^{T}$

          2. $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l = [\tilde{t}_{l1}, \tilde{t}_{l2}, ...,
          \tilde{t}_{ln}]^{T}$

          3. $\mathbf{t}_l = [\mathbf{t}_{l1}, \mathbf{t}_{l2}, ...,
          \mathbf{t}_{ln}]^{T}$

        output: >-
          In this section, we outline the essential aspects of the TWAS methods
          that will be referenced in our subsequent regression analysis (please
          consult the cited articles for further details). For clarity, let
          $\mathbf{y}$ denote a vector of traits for $n$ individuals, centered
          for convenience with no intercept required. Moreover, let
          $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$ represent the predicted gene expression for all
          individuals in tissue $l$, calculated as the sum of weighted genotype
          values from the SNPs in model $l$: $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l = \sum\_{a
          \in \mathrm{model}_l} w\_{a}^{l} X\_a$. Here, $X\_a$ signifies the
          genotype of SNP $a$, and $w\_{a}$ denotes its weight in the tissue
          prediction model $l$. Lastly, let $\mathbf{t}\_l$ denote the
          standardized version of $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}\_l$, with a mean of zero
          and a standard deviation of one.


          [Equation 1]: $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l = \sum\_{a \in \mathrm{model}_l}
          w\_{a}^{l} X\_a$


          [Equation 2]: $\mathbf{t}\_l = \frac{\tilde{\mathbf{t}}\_l -
          E[\tilde{\mathbf{t}}\_l]}{SD[\tilde{\mathbf{t}}\_l]}$


          Where $E[\tilde{\mathbf{t}}\_l]$ is the expected value and
          $SD[\tilde{\mathbf{t}}\_l]$ is the standard deviation of
          $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}\_l$. These calculations enable us to analyze gene
          expression patterns in relation to genetic associations, contributing
          to a better understanding of disease etiology and potential drug
          mechanisms.


          [References]

          [@pmid:33931583; @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]

          methods that will be referenced in our subsequent regression analysis

          In this section, we offer a brief overview of the TWAS methods used in
          our study, which will be further elaborated upon in the referenced
          articles. For clarity, let $\mathbf{y}$ denote a vector of traits for
          $n$ individuals, centered for convenience with no intercept required.
          We define $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$ as the predicted gene expression for
          all individuals in tissue $l$, calculated as the sum of weighted
          genotypes $X_a$ and their corresponding weights $w_{a}^{l}$ in the
          tissue prediction model $l$:


          \[\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l = \sum_{a \in \mathrm{model}_l} w_{a}^{l}
          X_{a}\]


          The standardized version of $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$, denoted as
          $\mathbf{t}_l$, is obtained by centering the mean at zero and scaling
          the standard deviation to one:


          \[\mathbf{t}_l = \frac{\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l - \mu_l}{\sigma_l}\]


          Here, $\mu_l$ represents the mean of $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$, and
          $\sigma_l$ denotes the standard deviation. The gene expression vectors
          for all tissues, $\mathbf{t}_1, \mathbf{t}_2, ..., \mathbf{t}_L$, form
          a matrix $\mathbf{T}$, where $L$ is the number of tissues.

          In this section, we provide a brief overview of the TWAS methods used
          in our study, which will be further explained in the referenced
          articles. For clarity, we define the following variables:

          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following

          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] represents a summarized
          version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the trait as
          a linear function of gene expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model given by equation (1) below:


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ denotes the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          determined by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          necessitates individual-level data to fit this model, while
          S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
          statistics through equation (2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$
          denotes the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue
          $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ represents the estimated effect size of SNP
          $a$ from the GWAS. In these Transcriptome-Wide Association Studies
          (TWAS) methods, genotype variances and covariances are consistently
          estimated using GTEx v8 [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the
          reference panel. Given that S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific
          directions of effects (for example, whether a higher or lower
          predicted expression of a gene confers more or less disease risk), we
          employed these $z$-scores in our drug repurposing strategy (described
          subsequently).

          reduce jargon, maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown
          formatting. Your revision should: 1) preserve the original information
          as much as possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve
          technical details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that
          equations (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly
          defined, 4) preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure
          most references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear
          in the original text; these references are crucial for academic
          integrity and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as
          "[@pmid:33931583; @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a simplified version
          of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the relationship
          between a trait and a gene's expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          Here, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
          regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denotes the error terms
          with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
          association is determined by calculating the $z$-score
          $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \text{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's
          tissue model $l$. PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this
          model, while S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
          GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\text{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          In this equation, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$,
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene
          in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated effect size
          of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In TWAS methods like S-PrediXcan, genotype
          variances and covariances are always estimated using the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific direction of effects (e.g., whether
          a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene is associated with
          more or less disease risk), we utilized these $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          S-PrediXcan represents a summarized version of PrediXcan, which models
          the trait as a linear function of a gene's expression in a single
          tissue using the univariate model described by equation (1) in the
          original manuscript [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1]. In this model,
          $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denote the error terms with
          variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association
          is determined by calculating the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l
          / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.
          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
          S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
          statistics [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. This approximation is achieved
          through equation (2) in the revised manuscript, which includes the
          variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_a$; the variance of the predicted
          expression of a gene in tissue $l$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$; and the
          estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS, $\hat{\beta}_a$. The
          standard error of $\hat{\beta}_a$ is denoted as
          $\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)$.


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          In tissue-wide association studies (TWAS) employing these methods,
          genotype variances and covariances are consistently estimated using
          the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. The advantage
          of S-PrediXcan lies in its ability to provide tissue-specific
          direction of effects, such as whether a higher or lower predicted
          expression of a gene confers more or less disease risk. These
          $z$-scores were instrumental in our drug repurposing approach
          (described below).

          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

        output: >-
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], a summarized version of
          the original PrediXcan method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models gene
          expression's influence on a trait as a linear function using the
          univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          Here, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
          regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ signifies error terms
          with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. To determine significance, a
          gene's tissue model $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) is calculated as:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l}=\frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

          $$


          PrediXcan requires individual-level data for fitting this model. In
          contrast, S-PrediXcan [@pmid:33931583;
          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225] approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores
          using only GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$,
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of a gene's predicted expression in
          tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated effect size of
          SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In TWAS methods, genotype variances and
          covariances are consistently estimated using GTEx v8
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel.


          S-PrediXcan's advantage lies in providing tissue-specific direction of
          effects, such as whether higher or lower predicted gene expressions
          are associated with increased or decreased disease risk. These
          $z$-scores were essential for our drug repurposing approach (described
          below).

          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression

          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /

        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan, as described in [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is a
          simplified version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. The former
          approximates PrediXcan's z-scores using only summary statistics from
          Genome-Wide Association Studies (GWAS), while the latter requires
          individual-level data to fit its model.


          PrediXcan models a trait as a linear function of a gene's expression
          in a single tissue, represented by equation (1) below:


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of association between a
          gene and a trait is determined by computing the z-score,
          $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$, for the
          tissue model $l$.


          S-PrediXcan uses equation (2) instead to calculate approximate
          z-scores:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          The genotype variances and covariances are always estimated using GTEx
          v8 [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel in these
          Transcriptome-Wide Association Studies (TWAS) methods.


          The advantage of S-PrediXcan lies in its ability to provide
          tissue-specific direction of effects, indicating whether a higher or
          lower predicted expression of a gene confers more or less disease
          risk. We utilized these z-scores in our drug repurposing approach,
          which will be described subsequently.

          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summarized version of
          the original PrediXcan method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. The PrediXcan
          model represents a trait as a linear function of a gene's expression
          in a single tissue using the univariate model given by equation (1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene
          in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated effect size
          of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In Tissue-specific Weighted Gene Score
          (TWAS) methods like S-PrediXcan, genotype variances and covariances

          (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel. The
          tissue-specific direction of effects provided by S-PrediXcan, such as
          whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene confers more
          or less disease risk, were essential for our drug repurposing approach
          (described below).


          Equation (1): Trait = Tissue-specific effect size * Expression + Error
          terms

          Equation (2): Approximate z-score = (weighted product of SNP effect
          sizes and their standard errors)

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/methods/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_17
      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], the summary version of
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], estimates the association between
          gene expression and a trait using linear models. In PrediXcan, the
          trait is modeled as a function of a single tissue's gene expression
          with the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          determined by calculating the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for each tissue model $l$.


          S-PrediXcan, on the other hand, approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores
          using only genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary statistics. It
          utilizes the following expression (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the predicted gene expression variance in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ represents the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from
          the GWAS. The genotype variances and covariances are always estimated
          using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel.


          S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific information on the direction of
          gene effects, such as whether a higher or lower predicted expression
          confers more or less disease risk. In our drug repurposing study
          (described below), we employed these $z$-scores to identify potential
          therapeutic targets.

          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association

          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l

          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is

      response:
        output: >-
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summary version of
          the original PrediXcan method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. Both methods
          model a trait as a linear function of gene expression in a single
          tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. PrediXcan requires individual-level data to
          fit this model, while S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan z-scores
          using only GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$,
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene
          in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated effect size
          of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel.


          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects, indicating
          whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene confers more
          or less disease risk. We employed these z-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below). In S-PrediXcan, the linear
          model is defined as:


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \sum_{a=1}^{n} w_a X_a + \bm{\epsilon},

          $$ {#eq:linmodel}


          where $w_a$ are weights, $X_a$ represents the genotype for SNP $a$,
          and $\bm{\epsilon}$ is the error term. The gene expression in tissue
          $l$ is predicted as:


          $$

          \hat{E}_g^l = \sum_{a=1}^{n} w_a^l X_a + \epsilon_l,

          $$ {#eq:predictedexpression}


          and the z-score for gene $g$ in tissue $l$ is calculated as:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{g,l} = \frac{\hat{E}_g^l - \bar{E}^l}{\sigma_l},

          $$ {#eq:zscore}


          where $\bar{E}^l$ is the mean expression level in tissue $l$ and
          $\sigma_l$ is its standard deviation.

          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summarized version
          of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the relationship
          between a trait and gene expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation 1) [@myref{eq:predixcan}]:


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
          tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association between a
          gene and a trait is determined by computing the $z$-score
          ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for the gene's tissue model ($l$). PrediXcan requires
          individual-level data to fit this model.


          In contrast, S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
          GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2) [@myref{eq:spredixcan}]:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          The genotype variances and covariances are always estimated using the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel.

          direction of effects, such as whether a higher or lower predicted
          expression of a gene confers more or less disease risk (Figure 1). In

          $z$-scores to identify potential therapeutic targets.

      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Your goal is to revise the
          following paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity,
          reduce jargon, maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown
          formatting. Your revision should: 1) preserve the original information
          as much as possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve
          technical details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that
          equations (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly
          defined, 4) preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure
          most references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear
          in the original text; these references are crucial for academic
          integrity and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as
          "[@pmid:33931583; @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/methods/prompts/candidate_with_metadata.txt
      vars: *ref_33
      response:
        output: >-
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], a summary version of the
          original method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models the relationship
          between a trait and gene expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ is the predicted gene expression in tissue $l$,
          $\gamma_l$ represents the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association between a
          gene and a trait is determined by calculating the $z$-score
          ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for the gene's tissue model ($l$). PrediXcan requires
          individual-level data to fit this model.


          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], an approximation of
          PrediXcan, calculates tissue-specific $z$-scores using only GWAS
          summary statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          In this equation, $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$,
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of predicted gene expression in
          tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated effect size of
          SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel.


          The advantage of S-PrediXcan is that it provides tissue-specific
          direction of effects, indicating whether higher or lower predicted
          gene expression in a tissue confers more or less disease risk. We
          utilized these $z$-scores in our drug repurposing approach (described
          below).


          Note: The equations and their references have been preserved as they
          appear in the original text.

      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan, as described by [doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is a
          simplified version of PrediXcan [doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
          models the trait as a linear function of gene expression in a single
          tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
          tissue $l$, $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association between a
          gene and a trait is determined by computing the $z$-score
          ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for the gene's tissue model ($l$). PrediXcan requires
          individual-level data to estimate this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only genome-wide association
          study (GWAS) summary statistics. This is achieved through Equation 2:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          In this equation, $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ denotes the variance of SNP $a$,
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted gene expression in
          tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ represents the estimated effect size
          of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In tissue-wide association studies (TWAS)
          employing these methods, genotype variances and covariances are always
          estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan
          provides tissue-specific direction of effects, allowing us to
          determine whether a higher or lower predicted gene expression confers
          more or less disease risk in our drug repurposing approach (described
          below).

          computing the $z$-score" to "The significance of the association is
          determined by computing the $z$-score".

          4. Added "In this equation," before Equation 2 for clarity.

          5. Replaced "These TWAS methods" with "In tissue-wide association
          studies (TWAS)" for clarity and added "employing these methods" to
          indicate that S-PrediXcan is used in TWAS.

          6. Added "allowing us to determine whether a higher or lower predicted
          gene expression confers more or less disease risk" to explain the
          significance of using $z$-scores in drug repurposing.

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ denotes the predicted gene expression in tissue

          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ comprises error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. To evaluate the significance of associations,
          the $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for a gene's tissue model ($l$) is
          computed as:


          $$

          S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary

          repurposing strategy (described below).

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], a summary version of the
          original PrediXcan method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models the
          relationship between a trait and gene expression in a single tissue
          using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
          tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denotes the error terms with
          variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association
          between a gene and a trait is determined by calculating the $z$-score
          ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for the tissue model ($l$) as:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l}=\frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

          $$


          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model. In
          contrast, S-PrediXcan [@pmid:33931583] approximates PrediXcan
          $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l

          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}

          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance

          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], the summary version of
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models a trait as a linear function
          of a gene's expression in a single tissue using the univariate model
          (Equation 1).


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          Here, $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
          tissue $l$, $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\epsilon_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. To assess significance, we compute the
          $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for a gene's tissue model ($l$) by dividing
          the estimated coefficient ($\hat{\gamma}_l$) by its standard error
          (se($\hat{\gamma}_l$)). For individual-level data analysis, PrediXcan
          uses this model.

          statistics (Equation 2).

          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of a gene's predicted expression in

          from the GWAS. S-PrediXcan methods always use the Genotype-Tissue

          $z$-scores, which provide tissue-specific direction of effects (e.g.,
          whether higher or lower predicted expression confers more or less
          disease risk). In our drug repurposing approach (described below), we
          employed these $z$-scores.

        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], the summarized version
          of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], estimates genetic associations
          with a trait based on gene expression patterns in specific tissues.
          PrediXcan models the relationship between a trait and a gene's
          expression in tissue $l$ using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
          tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denotes the error terms with
          variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. To assess the significance of this
          association, a $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) is computed as:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l}=\frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

          $$


          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit the model. In
          contrast, S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] approximates
          PrediXcan $z$-scores using only genome-wide association study (GWAS)
          summary statistics and gene expression data from the Genotype-Tissue
          Expression project (GTEx v8). S-PrediXcan calculates the approximate
          $z$-score for a gene in tissue $l$ as follows (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$
          represents the variance of the predicted gene expression in tissue
          $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated effect size of SNP $a$
          from the GWAS. The genotype variances and covariances are always
          estimated using GTEx v8 as a reference panel.


          The advantage of S-PrediXcan lies in its ability to provide
          tissue-specific direction of effects, such as whether a higher or
          lower predicted gene expression confers more or less disease risk
          (Figure 1). In our drug repurposing approach (described below), we
          utilized these $z$-scores to identify potential therapeutic targets
          and explore the mechanisms underlying complex traits.


          ![Figure 1: Overview of S-PrediXcan workflow](figure_1.png)

          --model ollama=mistral=7b-instruct-v0.2-fp16
      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity, reduce jargon,
          maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown formatting. Your
          revision should: 1) preserve the original information as much as
          possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve technical
          details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that equations
          (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly defined, 4)
          preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure most
          references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear in
          the original text; these references are crucial for academic integrity
          and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as "[@pmid:33931583;
          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/methods/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_33
      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan, as described in [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is a
          summarized version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
          models the trait as a linear function of gene expression in a single
          tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
          tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          determined by calculating the $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for each
          gene's tissue model ($l$).


          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
          S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only genome-wide
          association study (GWAS) summary statistics. This is accomplished
          through Equation 2:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$
          represents the variance of the predicted gene expression in tissue
          $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from
          the GWAS. In these transcriptome-wide association study (TWAS)
          methods, genotype variances and covariances are always estimated using
          the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel.


          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects, such as
          whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene confers more
          or less disease risk. Consequently, we employed the $z$-scores in our
          drug repurposing approach (described below).


          Equations:

          1. PrediXcan model for trait $\mathbf{y}$ as a function of gene
          expression in tissue $l$: $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l +
          \bm{\epsilon}_l$

          2. S-PrediXcan approximation of PrediXcan $z$-scores using GWAS
          summary statistics: $\hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)}$

          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summary version of
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the relationship
          between a trait and gene expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model given by equation (1) below:


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the gene's predicted expression in
          tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association between a
          gene and the trait in tissue $l$ is determined by computing the
          z-score, $\hat{z}_{l}$, for the gene's tissue model:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} = \frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\text{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

          $$ {#eq:zscore}


          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model. In
          contrast, S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan z-scores using only
          genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary statistics and equation
          (2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in \text{model}_l} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\text{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$,
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene
          in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP
          $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and covariances are always
          estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan
          provides tissue-specific direction of effects, indicating whether a
          higher or lower predicted expression of a gene confers more or less
          disease risk. As a result, we utilized these z-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], the summary version of
          this method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models a trait as a linear
          function of a gene's expression in a specific tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ is the gene's predicted expression in tissue $l$,
          $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          determined by calculating the $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for a gene's
          tissue model ($l$). PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit
          this model. In contrast, S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores
          using only Genome-Wide Association Study (GWAS) summary statistics and
          the expression (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          Here, $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of a gene's predicted expression in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the effect size estimate of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          S-PrediXcan uses the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel to estimate
          genotype variances and covariances.


          The advantage of using S-PrediXcan is its ability to provide
          tissue-specific directions of effects, such as whether a higher or
          lower predicted expression of a gene confers more or less disease
          risk. In our drug repurposing approach (described below), we employed
          these $z$-scores.

      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section.


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

        output: >-
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summarized version of
          the original PrediXcan model [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. The PrediXcan
          model represents a trait as a linear function of gene expression in a
          single tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1), where
          \(\mathbf{t}_l\) is the predicted gene expression in tissue \(l\),
          \(\beta_l\) is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient,
          and \(\epsilon_l\) are error terms with variance
          \(\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}\):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l.

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          The significance of the association between a gene and a trait is
          determined by calculating the \(z\)-score (\(\hat{z}_{l}\)) for each
          tissue model \(l\):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l}=\frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

          $$


          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41574-021-00693-x] approximates PrediXcan
          \(z\)-scores using GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where \(\hat{\Sigma}_a\) is the variance of SNP \(a\),
          \(\hat{\sigma}_l\) is the variance of gene expression in tissue \(l\),
          and \(\hat{\beta}_l\) is the estimated effect size of SNP \(a\) from
          the GWAS. In Tissue-specific Weighted Gene Expression (TWAS) methods,
          genotype variances and covariances are always estimated using the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel.


          S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific direction of effects, enabling us
          to determine whether higher or lower predicted gene expression in a
          tissue is associated with increased or decreased disease risk. We
          employed these \(z\)-scores in our drug repurposing approach
          (described below).


          Equation 1: PrediXcan model for a single tissue


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l.

          $$


          Equation 2: S-PrediXcan approximation of PrediXcan \(z\)-scores using
          GWAS summary statistics.

          of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models the trait as a
          linear function of the gene's expression on a single tissue using the
          univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summary version of
          the original PrediXcan method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of a gene's expression in a specific
          tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          determined by calculating the $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for a gene's
          tissue model ($l$). PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit
          this model. In contrast, S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41574-021-00698-8]
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only genome-wide association
          study (GWAS) summary statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          The genotype variances and covariances are always estimated using the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan
          provides tissue-specific direction of effects, allowing us to
          determine whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk. We employed these $z$-scores in our
          drug repurposing approach (described below).

          $$

          statistics.

          S-PrediXcan, as described in [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is a
          summarized version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
          models the trait as a linear function of gene expression in a single
          tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          }

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          Here, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
          regression coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with
          variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association
          is determined by calculating the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l
          / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.
          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model, while
          S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
          statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          In this equation, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$,
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene
          in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated effect size
          of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. These Transcriptome-Wide Association Study
          (TWAS) methods employ Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel to estimate
          genotype variances and covariances. Since S-PrediXcan offers
          tissue-specific direction of effects, such as whether a higher or
          lower predicted expression of a gene confers more or less disease
          risk, we utilized these $z$-scores in our drug repurposing approach
          (described below).

          tissue-specific effect size $\hat{\gamma}_l$ and error terms
          $\bm{\epsilon}_l$.

          using GWAS summary statistics.

          text of a scientific manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Your goal is to revise the
          following paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity,
          reduce jargon, maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown
          formatting. Your revision should: 1) preserve the original information
          as much as possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve
          technical details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that
          equations (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly
          defined, 4) preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure
          most references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear
          in the original text; these references are crucial for academic
          integrity and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as
          "[@pmid:33931583; @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a simplified version
          of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models a trait as a
          linear function of gene expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          }

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          determined by calculating the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \text{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          requires individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\text{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In TWAS methods like S-PrediXcan, genotype variances and covariances
          are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project
          (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific direction of effects, we employed
          these $z$-scores in our drug repurposing strategy (described below).

        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan, as outlined in [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is the
          summarized version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. In PrediXcan,
          we model a trait as a linear function of gene expression in a single
          tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          } {#eq:predixcan}

          $$


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
          regression coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denote error terms with
          variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. We assess the significance of the
          association by calculating the $z$-score, $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l
          / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$, for a gene's tissue model $l$.
          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model.


          In contrast, S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
          genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary statistics and the
          expression (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          } {#eq:spredixcan}

          $$


          Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ signifies the variance of SNP $a$,
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ represents the variance of the predicted expression
          of a gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated
          effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and
          covariances are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression
          project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference
          panel.


          S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific direction of effects, such as
          whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene confers more
          or less disease risk. We utilized these $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).
