      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity, reduce jargon,
          maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown formatting. Your
          revision should: 1) preserve the original information as much as
          possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve technical
          details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that equations
          (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly defined, 4)
          preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure most
          references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear in
          the original text; these references are crucial for academic integrity
          and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as "[@pmid:33931583;
          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

        display: >-

      response:
        output: >-
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], summarized as S-PrediXcan
          [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], is a method that models the relationship
          between gene expression and a trait using individual-level data
          [Equation (1)]. This model, represented by equation (1) below, treats
          the trait as a linear function of a gene's expression in a single
          tissue:


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,}

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
          regression coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denotes the error terms
          with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
          association is determined by computing the $z$-score,
          $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$, for a
          gene's tissue model $l$.


          S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
          statistics [Equation (2)] without requiring individual-level data.
          This approximation is given by:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          In this approach, the genotype variances and covariances are estimated
          using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel. S-PrediXcan
          provides tissue-specific direction of effects, which is crucial for
          our drug repurposing approach (described below). Here,
          $\hat{\sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$
          denotes the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue
          $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ signifies the estimated effect size of SNP
          $a$ from the GWAS.


          $$

          \text{[Equation (1):]} \quad \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l +
          \bm{\epsilon}_l,}

          \\

          \text{[Equation (2):]} \quad \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}}
          w_a^l \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)}.

          $$

          S-PrediXcan, as summarized in [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is a
          simplified version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
          models the trait as a linear function of gene expression in a single
          tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,}

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          determined by calculating the $z$-score, $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$, for each gene's tissue model $l$.
          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model. In
          contrast, S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
          GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          The genotype variances and covariances are always estimated using the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan
          provides tissue-specific direction of effects, indicating whether a
          higher or lower predicted expression of a gene is associated with
          increased or decreased disease risk. We employed these $z$-scores in

          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], a summary version of
          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models the relationship between a
          trait and gene expression in a single tissue using the univariate
          model (Equation 1). This model represents the trait as a linear
          function of the gene's expression, with error terms denoted by
          $\bm{\epsilon}_l$:


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,}

          \tag{Equation 1}

          $$


          Where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
          regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
          variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association
          between a gene and the trait is determined by calculating the
          $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for the tissue model ($l$) as follows:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} = \frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\text{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

          $$


          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to compute these
          coefficients, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores
          using only genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary statistics and
          the expression:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\text{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          \tag{Equation 2}

          $$

          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene
          in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated effect size

      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section.


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/methods/prompts/baseline.txt
      vars: *ref_49
      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summarized version
          of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the relationship
          between a trait and gene expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          }

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. To assess the significance of the association
          between a gene and the trait in this model, the $z$-score
          ($\hat{z}_{l}$) is computed as:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l}=\frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

          $$ {#eq:z-score}


          PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
          S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only genome-wide
          association study (GWAS) summary statistics and the expression:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In tissue-wide association studies (TWAS) using these methods,
          genotype variances and covariances are always estimated using the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan
          provides tissue-specific direction of effects, such as whether a
          higher or lower predicted expression of a gene confers more or less
          disease risk. Therefore, we utilized these $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /

          PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], the summarized version of
          the original PrediXcan method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models a trait
          as a linear function of gene expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation 1):


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          } {#eq:predixcan}

          $$


          Here, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
          regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with
          variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association
          is determined by calculating the $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for a
          gene's tissue model ($l$).


          To approximate PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
          statistics, S-PrediXcan (Equation 2) is employed:


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In Tissue-specific Weighted Gene Expression (TWAS) methods, genotype
          variances and covariances are always estimated using the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel.


          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects, such as

          or less disease risk. These $z$-scores were utilized in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

              $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}\_l$. These calculations enable us to analyze

              In this section, we offer a brief overview of the TWAS methods
              used in our study, which will be further elaborated upon in the
              referenced articles. For clarity, we denote $\mathbf{y}$ as a
              centered vector of traits for $n$ individuals, with no intercept
              required. The predicted expression for each gene across all
              individuals in tissue $l$ is represented by
              $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$, calculated as the sum of weighted genotype
              values $X_a$ and their corresponding weights $w_{a}^{l}$ from
              tissue prediction model $l$. Subsequently, we standardize this
              value to obtain $\mathbf{t}_l$, with a mean of zero and standard
              deviation of one.


              Equation (1) below defines the weighted sum of genotypes for
              individual $i$ in tissue $l$:


              $$ \tilde{t}_{il} = \sum_{a \in \mathrm{model}_l} w_{a}^{l} X_{ia}
              $$


              And equation (2) shows how we standardize the predicted
              expression:


              $$ t_{il} = \frac{\tilde{t}_{il} - \mu_l}{\sigma_l} $$


              Where $\mu_l$ and $\sigma_l$ denote the mean and standard
              deviation of $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$, respectively.

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] represents a
              summarized version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which
              models the trait as a linear function of gene expression in a
              single tissue using the univariate model given by equation (1)
              below:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ denotes the estimated effect size or
              regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is determined by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan necessitates individual-level
              data to fit this model, while S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics through equation
              (2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ denotes the variance of the predicted expression
              of a gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ represents the
              estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these
              Transcriptome-Wide Association Studies (TWAS) methods, genotype
              variances and covariances are consistently estimated using GTEx v8
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Given that
              S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific directions of effects (for
              example, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we employed these $z$-scores
              in our drug repurposing strategy (described subsequently).

              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the
              relationship between a trait and a gene's expression in a single
              tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              Here, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
              regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denotes the error

              the association is determined by calculating the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \text{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan requires individual-level data

              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}

            assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
            \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.

            S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS

            \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}

            where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$

              ---

              S-PrediXcan represents a summarized version of PrediXcan, which
              models the trait as a linear function of a gene's expression in a
              single tissue using the univariate model described by equation (1)
              in the original manuscript [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1]. In
              this model, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size
              or regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denote the error
              terms with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of
              the association is determined by calculating the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan requires individual-level data
              to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
              [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. This approximation is achieved through
              equation (2) in the revised manuscript, which includes the
              variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_a$; the variance of the
              predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$;
              and the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS,
              $\hat{\beta}_a$. The standard error of $\hat{\beta}_a$ is denoted
              as $\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)$.


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              In tissue-wide association studies (TWAS) employing these methods,
              genotype variances and covariances are consistently estimated
              using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. The
              advantage of S-PrediXcan lies in its ability to provide
              tissue-specific direction of effects, such as whether a higher or
              lower predicted expression of a gene confers more or less disease

              approach (described below).

              terms with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. To determine

              expression in a single tissue, represented by equation (1) below:


              $$

              Error terms

              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan needs individual-level data to
              fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

            text: >-
              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], the summary version
              of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], estimates the association
              between gene expression and a trait using linear models. In
              PrediXcan, the trait is modeled as a function of a single tissue's
              gene expression with the univariate model (Equation 1):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
              determined by calculating the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for
              each tissue model $l$.


              S-PrediXcan, on the other hand, approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores
              using only genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary
              statistics. It utilizes the following expression (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the predicted gene expression variance in
              tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ represents the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and
              covariances are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue
              Expression project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a
              reference panel.


              S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific information on the direction of
              gene effects, such as whether a higher or lower predicted
              expression confers more or less disease risk. In our drug
              repurposing study (described below), we employed these $z$-scores
              to identify potential therapeutic targets.

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}

              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$


              with $\hat{\sigma}_a$ being the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ the estimated effect size
              of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In our tissue-wide association studies
              (TWAS), genotype variances and covariances are consistently
              estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. The
              advantage of S-PrediXcan is its ability to provide tissue-specific
              directions of effect, such as whether a higher or lower predicted
              expression of a gene confers more or less disease risk.
              Consequently, we utilized these $z$-scores in our drug repurposing
              approach (described below).

            text: >-
              Failed to find the following keywords:
               - \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)
              ---

              PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summary version
              of the original PrediXcan method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. Both
              methods model a trait as a linear function of gene expression in a
              single tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. PrediXcan requires individual-level data
              to fit this model, while S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              z-scores using only GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the estimated
              effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and
              covariances are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue
              Expression project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the
              reference panel.


              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects,
              indicating whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a
              gene confers more or less disease risk. We employed these z-scores
              in our drug repurposing approach (described below). In
              S-PrediXcan, the linear model is defined as:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \sum_{a=1}^{n} w_a X_a + \bm{\epsilon},

              $$ {#eq:linmodel}


              where $w_a$ are weights, $X_a$ represents the genotype for SNP
              $a$, and $\bm{\epsilon}$ is the error term. The gene expression in
              tissue $l$ is predicted as:


              $$

              \hat{E}_g^l = \sum_{a=1}^{n} w_a^l X_a + \epsilon_l,

              $$ {#eq:predictedexpression}


              and the z-score for gene $g$ in tissue $l$ is calculated as:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{g,l} = \frac{\hat{E}_g^l - \bar{E}^l}{\sigma_l},

              $$ {#eq:zscore}


              where $\bar{E}^l$ is the mean expression level in tissue $l$ and
              $\sigma_l$ is its standard deviation.

              S-PrediXcan, as described by [doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is
              a simplified version of PrediXcan [doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of gene expression in a
              single tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
              tissue $l$, $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association
              between a gene and a trait is determined by computing the
              $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for the gene's tissue model ($l$).
              PrediXcan requires individual-level data to estimate this model,
              whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
              genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary statistics. This is
              achieved through Equation 2:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              In this equation, $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ denotes the variance of SNP
              $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted gene
              expression in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ represents the
              estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In tissue-wide
              association studies (TWAS) employing these methods, genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan
              provides tissue-specific direction of effects, allowing us to
              determine whether a higher or lower predicted gene expression
              confers more or less disease risk in our drug repurposing approach
              (described below).


              Here's a breakdown of the changes made:


              1. Added introductory sentence for clarity.

              2. Replaced "PrediXcan models the trait as" with "PrediXcan is
              modeled as".

              3. Changed "The significance of the association is assessed by
              computing the $z$-score" to "The significance of the association
              is determined by computing the $z$-score".

              4. Added "In this equation," before Equation 2 for clarity.

              5. Replaced "These TWAS methods" with "In tissue-wide association
              studies (TWAS)" for clarity and added "employing these methods" to
              indicate that S-PrediXcan is used in TWAS.

              6. Added "allowing us to determine whether a higher or lower
              predicted gene expression confers more or less disease risk" to
              explain the significance of using $z$-scores in drug repurposing.

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summarized
              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the
              relationship between a trait and gene expression in a single
              tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1)
              [@myref{eq:predixcan}]:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$


              where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
              tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association
              between a gene and a trait is determined by calculating the
              $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for each tissue model ($l$) as follows:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} = \frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

              $$


              PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit the gene
              expression models, while S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary
              statistics [@myref{doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776},
              @myref{doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1}]. In S-PrediXcan, the
              genotype variances and covariances are estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@myref{doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776}] as a reference panel
              (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$


              where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted gene expression
              in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of
              SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The use of S-PrediXcan $z$-scores enables

            text: >-
              Failed to fix the following expressions:
               - $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ -> $\hat{\sigma}_a$
              ---

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], the summarized
              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], estimates genetic
              associations with a trait based on gene expression patterns in
              specific tissues. PrediXcan models the relationship between a
              trait and a gene's expression in tissue $l$ using the univariate
              model (Equation 1):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
              tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denotes the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. To assess the significance of
              this association, a $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) is computed as:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l}=\frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

              $$


              PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit the model. In
              contrast, S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] approximates
              PrediXcan $z$-scores using only genome-wide association study
              (GWAS) summary statistics and gene expression data from the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8). S-PrediXcan
              calculates the approximate $z$-score for a gene in tissue $l$ as
              follows (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ represents the variance of the predicted gene
              expression in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ denotes the
              estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using GTEx v8 as a
              reference panel.


              The advantage of S-PrediXcan lies in its ability to provide
              tissue-specific direction of effects, such as whether a higher or
              lower predicted gene expression confers more or less disease risk
              (Figure 1). In our drug repurposing approach (described below), we
              utilized these $z$-scores to identify potential therapeutic
              targets and explore the mechanisms underlying complex traits.


              ![Figure 1: Overview of S-PrediXcan workflow](figure_1.png)

              with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as "[@pmid:33931583;

              Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is
              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
              $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient,
              and $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
              assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
              \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.
              PrediXcan needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
              S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
              summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              S-PrediXcan, as outlined in [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is
              a summarized version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367].
              PrediXcan models the trait as a linear function of gene expression
              in a single tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1).


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              Here, $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
              tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with variance
              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
              determined by calculating the z-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for a gene's
              tissue model ($l$).


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} = \frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}

              $$


              PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model,
              whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan z-scores using only
              GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2).


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              In this equation, $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP
              $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted gene
              expression in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated
              effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and
              covariances are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue
              Expression project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the
              reference panel.


              The advantage of S-PrediXcan lies in its ability to provide
              tissue-specific direction of effects, such as whether a higher or

              The PrediXcan model represents a trait as a linear function of
              gene expression in a single tissue using the univariate model
              (Equation 1), where \(\mathbf{t}_l\) is the predicted gene
              expression in tissue \(l\), \(\beta_l\) is the estimated effect
              size or regression coefficient, and \(\epsilon_l\) are error terms
              with variance \(\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}\):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l.

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              The significance of the association between a gene and a trait is
              determined by calculating the \(z\)-score (\(\hat{z}_{l}\)) for
              each tissue model \(l\):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l}=\frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

              $$


              PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model,
              whereas S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41574-021-00693-x] approximates
              PrediXcan \(z\)-scores using GWAS summary statistics (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where \(\hat{\Sigma}_a\) is the variance of SNP \(a\),
              \(\hat{\sigma}_l\) is the variance of gene expression in tissue
              \(l\), and \(\hat{\beta}_l\) is the estimated effect size of SNP
              \(a\) from the GWAS. In Tissue-specific Weighted Gene Expression
              (TWAS) methods, genotype variances and covariances are always
              estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel.


              S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific direction of effects, enabling
              us to determine whether higher or lower predicted gene expression
              in a tissue is associated with increased or decreased disease

              approach (described below).

            $$ {#eq:predixcan}


            where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
            $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient,
            and $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
            $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
            assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
            \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.
            PrediXcan needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
            S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
            summary statistics with the expression


            $$

            \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
            \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
            \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

            $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


            where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$
            is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$,
            and $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the
            GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances
            are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project
            (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel.
            Since S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
            instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
            confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
            drug repurposing approach (described below).

              PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a summary version
              of the original PrediXcan method [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of a gene's expression in a
              specific tissue using the univariate model (Equation 1):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is determined by calculating the $z$-score
              ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for a gene's tissue model ($l$). PrediXcan
              requires individual-level data to fit this model. In contrast,
              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41574-021-00698-8] approximates
              PrediXcan $z$-scores using only genome-wide association study
              (GWAS) summary statistics (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and
              covariances are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue
              Expression project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the
              reference panel. S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of
              effects, allowing us to determine whether a higher or lower
              predicted expression of a gene confers more or less disease risk.

              (described below).

              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In TWAS methods like S-PrediXcan,
              genotype variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan offers tissue-specific direction of effects, we
              employed these $z$-scores in our drug repurposing strategy
              (described below).


              [Equation 1]: $$\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l +
              \bm{\epsilon}_l}$$

              [Equation 2]: $$\hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\text{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)}$$

              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression

              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the

              S-PrediXcan, as outlined in [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], is
              the summarized version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. In
              PrediXcan, we model a trait as a linear function of gene
              expression in a single tissue using the univariate model (Equation
              1):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              } {#eq:predixcan}

              $$


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
              regression coefficient and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ denote error terms
              with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. We assess the significance
              of the association by calculating the $z$-score,
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$, for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan requires individual-level data
              to fit this model.

              only genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary statistics and
              the expression (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              } {#eq:spredixcan}

              $$

              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)

            S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the summary version

            linear function of the gene's expression on a single tissue using
            the univariate model


            $$

            \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

            $$ {#eq:predixcan}


            where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
            coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
            $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
            assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
            \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.
            PrediXcan needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
            S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
            summary statistics with the expression


            $$

            \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l

            \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

            $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


            where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$
            is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$,
            and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the
            GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances
            are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project
            (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel.
            Since S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
            instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
            confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
            drug repurposing approach (described below).

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], a summary version
              of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models the relationship
              between a trait and gene expression in a single tissue using the
              univariate model given by equation (1) in the manuscript:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association between a gene and the trait in tissue $l$ is
              determined by calculating the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$.
              PrediXcan requires individual-level data for fitting this model,
              while S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
              genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary statistics and the
              expression:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In tissue-wide association studies
              (TWAS) methods, genotype variances and covariances are estimated
              using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects, we
              utilized these $z$-scores in our drug repurposing approach

              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,}

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression

              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
              determined by calculating the $z$-score,

              data to fit this model. In contrast, S-PrediXcan approximates
              PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics (Equation
              2):

              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}

              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a

              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. The genotype variances and
              covariances are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue
              Expression project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the
              reference panel. S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of
              effects, indicating whether a higher or lower predicted expression
              of a gene is associated with increased or decreased disease risk.

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], a summary version
              of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models the relationship
              between a trait and gene expression in a single tissue using the
              univariate model (Equation 1). This model represents the trait as
              a linear function of the gene's expression, with error terms
              denoted by $\bm{\epsilon}_l$:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,}

              \tag{Equation 1}

              $$


              Where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
              regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms
              with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association between a gene and the trait is determined by
              calculating the $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for the tissue model
              ($l$) as follows:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} = \frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\text{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}.

              $$

              $z$-scores using only genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary
              statistics and the expression:

              \tag{Equation 2}

              Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is
              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan needs individual-level data to
              fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              Failed to fix the following expressions:

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1], the summary version
              of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models a trait as a linear
              function of a gene's expression in a single tissue using the
              univariate model (Equation 1):


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,}

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association between a gene and a trait is assessed by computing
              the $z$-score ($\hat{z}_{l}$) for that gene's tissue model ($l$).
              PrediXcan requires individual-level data to fit this model,
              whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
              genome-wide association study (GWAS) summary statistics and the
              expression (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In this transcriptome-wide
              association study (TWAS) approach, genotype variances and
              covariances are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue
              Expression project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the
              reference panel. Since S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific
              direction of effects (e.g., whether a higher or lower predicted
              expression of a gene confers more or less disease risk), we
              employed these $z$-scores in our drug repurposing strategy
              (described below).


              {#eq:predixcan}: PrediXcan univariate model for a trait as a
              linear function of gene expression on a single tissue.


              {#eq:spredixcan}: S-PrediXcan approximation of PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using GWAS summary statistics.
